## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in materials science and solid mechanics. The relationship captures how materials deform under load at different temperatures, involving elasticity, plasticity, thermal softening, and potentially creep or viscoelastic effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (elastic modulus varying linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening in plastic deformation, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Hollomon equation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (empirical power-law stress-strain for metals)
- Johnson-Cook strength model (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T)**c4 (strain hardening with temperature-dependent softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (elastic modulus with Arrhenius-like temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation-type stress-strain curve)
- Temperature-dependent Voce: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effects)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Temperature-dependent Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T + c4 * T**2) (Ludwik with polynomial thermal correction)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening, avoids zero-strain singularity)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Coupled polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 + c3 * T (bilinear coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) multiplying strain-dependent terms
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), or rational form epsilon/(epsilon+c)
- Power-law strain hardening → sigma ~ epsilon**n where 0 < n < 1 indicates work hardening in metals
- Additive yield stress → Constant offset c0 + f(epsilon) separating elastic yield point from hardening contribution
- Temperature-strain separability → Product form sigma = g(epsilon) * h(T) when thermal and mechanical effects are decoupled
- Polynomial temperature dependence of modulus → E(T) = c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2 reflecting gradual thermal softening
- Phase transition or melting effects → Sharp nonlinearity in T dependence, e.g., tanh(c0*(T - c1)) for transition regions
- Creep/rate-independent thermal activation → Arrhenius-type factor exp(c0/T) modulating flow stress at elevated temperatures
